   <h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading">Transnistria</h1> 
   <div id="bodyContent" class="vector-body"> 
    <div id="siteSub" class="noprint">
     From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia
    </div> 
    <div id="contentSub"></div> 
    <div id="contentSub2"></div> 
    <div id="jump-to-nav"></div> <a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a> <a class="mw-jump-link" href="#searchInput">Jump to search</a> 
    <div id="mw-content-text" class="mw-body-content mw-content-ltr" lang="en" dir="ltr">
     <div class="mw-parser-output">
      <div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">
       Breakaway state in Eastern Europe that has declared independence from Moldova
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       This article is about the post-Soviet breakaway republic. For the administrative unit of Moldova, see <a href="/wiki/Transnistria_autonomous_territorial_unit" title="Transnistria autonomous territorial unit">Transnistria autonomous territorial unit</a>. For the Romanian administrative unit during World War II, see <a href="/wiki/Transnistria_Governorate" title="Transnistria Governorate">Transnistria Governorate</a>. For the geographical region, see <a href="/wiki/Transnistria_(region)" title="Transnistria (region)">Transnistria (region)</a>.
      </div> 
      <p class="mw-empty-elt"> </p> 
      <table class="infobox geography vcard" style="font-size:88%;">

      <p><b>Transnistria</b>, officially the <b>Pridnestrovian Moldavian Republic</b> (<b>PMR</b>),<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[a]</a></sup> is a <a href="/wiki/List_of_states_with_limited_recognition" title="List of states with limited recognition">breakaway state</a> in the narrow strip of land between the river <a href="/wiki/Dniester" title="Dniester">Dniester</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukrainian</a> border that is internationally recognized as part of <a href="/wiki/Moldova" title="Moldova">Moldova</a>. Its capital is <a href="/wiki/Tiraspol" title="Tiraspol">Tiraspol</a>. Transnistria <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Transnistria" title="Foreign relations of Transnistria">has been recognised</a> only by three other mostly unrecognised breakaway states: <a href="/wiki/Abkhazia" title="Abkhazia">Abkhazia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Artsakh" title="Republic of Artsakh">Artsakh</a>, and <a href="/wiki/South_Ossetia" title="South Ossetia">South Ossetia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[8]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Transnistria is designated by the Republic of Moldova as the <a href="/wiki/Transnistria_autonomous_territorial_unit_with_special_legal_status" class="mw-redirect" title="Transnistria autonomous territorial unit with special legal status">Transnistria autonomous territorial unit with special legal status</a> (<a href="/wiki/Romanian_language" title="Romanian language">Romanian</a>: <i lang="ro">Unitatea teritorială autonomă cu statut juridic special Transnistria</i>),<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[9]</a></sup> or <i lang="ro" title="Romanian-language text">Stînga Nistrului</i> ("Left Bank of the Dniester").<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[10]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[11]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[12]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>After the <a href="/wiki/Dissolution_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Dissolution of the Soviet Union">dissolution of the Soviet Union</a>, tensions between Moldova and the breakaway Transnistrian territory <a href="/wiki/Transnistria_War" title="Transnistria War">escalated into a military conflict</a> that started in March 1992 and was concluded by a ceasefire in July of the same year. As part of that agreement, a three-party (Russia, Moldova, Transnistria) <a href="/wiki/Joint_Control_Commission" title="Joint Control Commission">Joint Control Commission</a> supervises the security arrangements in the <a href="/wiki/Demilitarised_zone" class="mw-redirect" title="Demilitarised zone">demilitarised zone</a>, comprising twenty localities on both sides of the river. Although the ceasefire has held, the territory's political status remains unresolved: Transnistria is an unrecognised but <i><a href="/wiki/De_facto" title="De facto">de facto</a></i> independent <a href="/wiki/Semi-presidential_republic" class="mw-redirect" title="Semi-presidential republic">semi-presidential republic</a> with its own <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Transnistria" title="Government of Transnistria">government</a>, <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_Transnistria" class="mw-redirect" title="Parliament of Transnistria">parliament</a>, <a href="/wiki/Military_of_Transnistria" class="mw-redirect" title="Military of Transnistria">military</a>, <a href="/wiki/Law_enforcement_in_Transnistria" title="Law enforcement in Transnistria">police</a>, postal system, <a href="/wiki/Transnistrian_ruble" title="Transnistrian ruble">currency</a> and vehicle registration.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[13]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[14]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[15]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-DFSTATES_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DFSTATES-17">[16]</a></sup> Its authorities have adopted a <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Transnistria" title="Constitution of Transnistria">constitution</a>, <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Transnistria" title="Flag of Transnistria">flag</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anthem_of_Transnistria" title="Anthem of Transnistria">national anthem</a> and <a href="/wiki/Coat_of_arms_of_Transnistria" title="Coat of arms of Transnistria">coat of arms</a>. </p>
      <p>After a 2005 agreement between Moldova and Ukraine, all Transnistrian companies that seek to export goods through the Ukrainian border <a href="/wiki/Transnistrian_border_customs_issues" title="Transnistrian border customs issues">must be registered with the Moldovan authorities</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[17]</a></sup> This agreement was implemented after the <a href="/wiki/European_Union_Border_Assistance_Mission_to_Moldova_and_Ukraine" title="European Union Border Assistance Mission to Moldova and Ukraine">European Union Border Assistance Mission to Moldova and Ukraine</a> (EUBAM) took force in 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[18]</a></sup> Most Transnistrians have Moldovan citizenship,<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[19]</a></sup> but many also have Russian, Romanian, or Ukrainian citizenship.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[20]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[21]</a></sup> The main ethnic groups are Russians, Moldovans, and Ukrainians. </p>
      <p>Transnistria, <a href="/wiki/Abkhazia" title="Abkhazia">Abkhazia</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Ossetia" title="South Ossetia">South Ossetia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Artsakh" title="Republic of Artsakh">Artsakh</a> are post-Soviet "<a href="/wiki/Frozen_conflict" title="Frozen conflict">frozen conflict</a>" zones.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[22]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[23]</a></sup> These four partially recognised states maintain friendly relations with each other and form the <a href="/wiki/Community_for_Democracy_and_Rights_of_Nations" title="Community for Democracy and Rights of Nations">Community for Democracy and Rights of Nations</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Абхазия,_Южная_Осетия_и_Приднестровье_признали_независимость_друг_друга_и_призвали_всех_к_этому_же_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Абхазия,_Южная_Осетия_и_Приднестровье_признали_независимость_друг_друга_и_призвали_всех_к_этому_же-25">[24]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[25]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[26]</a></sup> </p>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Names">Names</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Transnistria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Names">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Names_of_Transnistria" title="Names of Transnistria">Names of Transnistria</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The region can also be referred to in English as <i>Trans-Dniester</i><sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[27]</a></sup> or <i>Transdniestria</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[28]</a></sup> These names are adaptations of the Romanian colloquial name of the region, <i>Transnistria</i>, meaning "beyond the Dniester River". </p>
      <p>The documents of the government of Moldova refer to the region as <i lang="ro" title="Romanian-language text">Stînga Nistrului</i> (in full, <i lang="ro" title="Romanian-language text">Unitățile Administrativ-Teritoriale din Stînga Nistrului</i>) meaning "Left Bank of the Dniester" (in full, "Administrative-territorial unit(s) of the Left Bank of the Dniester"). </p>
      <p>According to the Transnistrian authorities, the name of the state is the "Pridnestrovian Moldavian Republic" (PMR) (<a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">Russian</a>: <span lang="ru">Приднестровская Молдавская Республика, ПМР</span>, <i lang="ru-Latn" title="Russian-language text">Pridnestrovskaya Moldavskaya Respublika</i>; <a href="/wiki/Moldovan_Cyrillic_alphabet" title="Moldovan Cyrillic alphabet">Moldovan Cyrillic alphabet</a>: <span lang="ro" title="Romanian-language text">Република Молдовеняскэ Нистрянэ, РМН</span>, <i lang="ro" title="Romanian-language text">Republica Moldovenească Nistreană</i>; <a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_language" title="Ukrainian language">Ukrainian</a>: <span lang="uk">Придністровська Молдавська Республіка, ПМР</span>, <i lang="uk-Latn" title="Ukrainian-language text">Prydnistrovska Moldavska Respublika</i>). The short form is <i lang="ru-Latn" title="Russian-language text">Pridnestrovye</i> (<a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">Russian</a>: <span lang="ru">Приднестровье</span>; <a href="/wiki/Moldovan_Cyrillic_alphabet" title="Moldovan Cyrillic alphabet">Moldovan Cyrillic alphabet</a>: <span lang="ro" title="Romanian-language text">Нистрения</span>,<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[29]</a></sup> <i lang="ro" title="Romanian-language text">Nistrenia</i>; <a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_language" title="Ukrainian language">Ukrainian</a>: <span lang="uk">Придністров'я</span>, <i lang="uk-Latn" title="Ukrainian-language text">Prydnistrovia</i>), meaning "[land] by the Dniester". </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Transnistria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Transnistria" title="History of Transnistria">History of Transnistria</a>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Soviet_and_Romanian_administration">Soviet and Romanian administration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Transnistria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Soviet and Romanian administration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Moldavian_Autonomous_Soviet_Socialist_Republic" title="Moldavian Autonomous Soviet Socialist Republic">Moldavian Autonomous Soviet Socialist Republic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Moldavian_SSR" class="mw-redirect" title="Moldavian SSR">Moldavian SSR</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Romania_MASSR_1924.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Romania_MASSR_1924.png/220px-Romania_MASSR_1924.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="161" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Romania_MASSR_1924.png/330px-Romania_MASSR_1924.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Romania_MASSR_1924.png/440px-Romania_MASSR_1924.png 2x" data-file-width="585" data-file-height="428"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Romania_MASSR_1920.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Moldavian_ASSR" class="mw-redirect" title="Moldavian ASSR">Moldavian ASSR</a> (orange) and Romania, 1924–1940
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Transnistria became an autonomous political entity in 1924 with the proclamation of the <a href="/wiki/Moldavian_ASSR" class="mw-redirect" title="Moldavian ASSR">Moldavian ASSR</a>, which included today's Transnistria (4,100&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (1,600&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi)) and an adjacent area (4,200&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (1,600&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi)) around the city of <a href="/wiki/Balta,_Odessa_Oblast" title="Balta, Odessa Oblast">Balta</a> in modern-day <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukraine</a>, but nothing from <a href="/wiki/Bessarabia" title="Bessarabia">Bessarabia</a>, which at the time formed part of <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Romania" title="Kingdom of Romania">Romania</a>. One of the reasons for the creation of the Moldavian ASSR was the desire of the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a> at the time to eventually incorporate Bessarabia.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The Moldavian SSR, organised by a decision of the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Soviet_of_the_USSR" class="mw-redirect" title="Supreme Soviet of the USSR">Supreme Soviet of the USSR</a> on 2 August 1940, was formed out of a part of Bessarabia (<a href="/wiki/June_1940_Soviet_Ultimatum" class="mw-redirect" title="June 1940 Soviet Ultimatum">taken from Romania</a> on 28 June, after the <a href="/wiki/Molotov%E2%80%93Ribbentrop_Pact" title="Molotov–Ribbentrop Pact">Molotov–Ribbentrop Pact</a>) and out of a part of the Moldavian ASSR roughly equivalent to present-day Transnistria. </p>
      <p>In 1941, after <a href="/wiki/Axis_powers" title="Axis powers">Axis forces</a> invaded the Soviet Union during the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Front_(World_War_II)" title="Eastern Front (World War II)">Second World War</a>, they defeated the Soviet troops in the region and occupied it. Romania controlled the entire region between Dniester and <a href="/wiki/Southern_Bug" title="Southern Bug">Southern Bug</a> rivers, including the city of <a href="/wiki/Odessa" title="Odessa">Odessa</a> as local capital.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[30]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Romanian-administered territory, known as the <a href="/wiki/Transnistria_Governorate" title="Transnistria Governorate">Transnistria Governorate</a>, with an area of 39,733&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (15,341&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi) and a population of 2.3 million inhabitants, was divided into 13 counties: Ananiev, Balta, Berzovca, Dubasari, Golta, Jugastru, Movilau, Oceacov, Odessa, <a href="/wiki/Ovidiopol" title="Ovidiopol">Ovidiopol</a>, Rîbnița, Tiraspol and Tulcin. This enlarged Transnistria was home to nearly 200,000 Romanian-speaking residents. </p>
      <p>The Romanian administration of Transnistria attempted to stabilise the situation in the area under Romanian control, implementing a process of <a href="/wiki/Romanianization" title="Romanianization">Romanianization</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[31]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>During the Romanian occupation of 1941–44, between 150,000 and 250,000 Ukrainian and Romanian Jews were deported to Transnistria; the majority were <a href="/wiki/Einsatzgruppen" title="Einsatzgruppen">executed</a> or died from other causes in ghettos and concentration camps of the Governorate.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[32]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>After the <a href="/wiki/Red_Army" title="Red Army">Red Army</a> reconquered the area in 1944, Soviet authorities executed, exiled or imprisoned hundreds of inhabitants of the Moldavian SSR in the following months on charges of collaboration with the "German-fascist occupiers". A later campaign was directed against the rich peasant families, who were deported to <a href="/wiki/Kazakhstan" title="Kazakhstan">Kazakhstan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Siberia" title="Siberia">Siberia</a>. Over the course of two days, 6–7 July 1949, a plan named "Operation South" saw the deportation of over 11,342 families by order of the Moldovian Minister of State Security, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Iosif_Mordovets&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Iosif Mordovets (page does not exist)">Iosif Mordovets</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[33]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Secession">Secession</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Transnistria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Secession">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Igor_Smirnov.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Igor_Smirnov.jpg/220px-Igor_Smirnov.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="164" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/0/08/Igor_Smirnov.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="297" data-file-height="222"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Igor_Smirnov.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Igor_Smirnov" title="Igor Smirnov">Igor Smirnov</a>, first president of Transnistria from 1991 to 2011
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In the 1980s, <a href="/wiki/Mikhail_Gorbachev" title="Mikhail Gorbachev">Mikhail Gorbachev</a>'s policies of <a href="/wiki/Perestroika" title="Perestroika">perestroika</a> and <a href="/wiki/Glasnost" title="Glasnost">glasnost</a> in the Soviet Union allowed political liberalisation at a regional level. This led to the creation of various informal movements all over the country, and to a rise of nationalism within most Soviet republics. In the Moldavian SSR in particular, there was a significant resurgence of pro-Romanian nationalism among Moldovans.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[34]</a></sup> The most prominent of these movements was the <a href="/wiki/Popular_Front_of_Moldova" title="Popular Front of Moldova">Popular Front of Moldova</a>. In early 1988, PFM demanded that the Soviet authorities declare <a href="/wiki/Moldovan_language" title="Moldovan language">Moldovan</a> the only state language, return to the use of the Latin alphabet, and recognise the shared ethnic identity of Moldovans and Romanians. The more radical factions of the Popular Front espoused extreme anti-minority, ethnocentric and chauvinist positions,<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[35]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[36]</a></sup> calling for minority populations, particularly the Slavs (mainly Russians and Ukrainians) and <a href="/wiki/Gagauz_people" title="Gagauz people">Gagauz</a>, to leave or be expelled from Moldova.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[37]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On 31 August 1989, the Supreme Soviet of the Moldavian SSR adopted Moldovan as the only official language with <a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">Russian</a> retained only for secondary purposes, returned Moldovan to the <a href="/wiki/Latin_alphabet" title="Latin alphabet">Latin alphabet</a>, and declared a shared Moldovan-Romanian linguistic identity. As plans for major cultural changes in Moldova were made public, tensions rose further. Ethnic minorities felt threatened by the prospects of removing Russian as the <a href="/wiki/Official_language" title="Official language">official language</a>, which served as the medium of interethnic communication, and by the possible future reunification of Moldova and Romania, as well as the ethnocentric rhetoric of the Popular Front. The Yedinstvo (Unity) Movement, established by the Slavic population of Moldova, pressed for equal status to be given to both Russian and Moldovan.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[38]</a></sup> Transnistria's ethnic and linguistic composition differed significantly from most of the rest of Moldova. The share of ethnic Russians and Ukrainians was especially high and an overall majority of the population, some of them Moldovans, spoke Russian as a mother tongue.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[39]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Billboard_Commemorating_1990-2017_Independence_-_Tiraspol_-_Transnistria_(36032671973).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Billboard_Commemorating_1990-2017_Independence_-_Tiraspol_-_Transnistria_%2836032671973%29.jpg/220px-Billboard_Commemorating_1990-2017_Independence_-_Tiraspol_-_Transnistria_%2836032671973%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Billboard_Commemorating_1990-2017_Independence_-_Tiraspol_-_Transnistria_%2836032671973%29.jpg/330px-Billboard_Commemorating_1990-2017_Independence_-_Tiraspol_-_Transnistria_%2836032671973%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Billboard_Commemorating_1990-2017_Independence_-_Tiraspol_-_Transnistria_%2836032671973%29.jpg/440px-Billboard_Commemorating_1990-2017_Independence_-_Tiraspol_-_Transnistria_%2836032671973%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3648" data-file-height="2736"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Billboard_Commemorating_1990-2017_Independence_-_Tiraspol_-_Transnistria_(36032671973).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet</a> symbols are used in Transnistria.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The nationalist Popular Front won the first free parliamentary elections in the Moldavian SSR in early 1990,<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[40]</a></sup> and its agenda started slowly to be implemented. On 2 September 1990, the <a href="/wiki/Pridnestrovian_Moldavian_Soviet_Socialist_Republic" title="Pridnestrovian Moldavian Soviet Socialist Republic">Pridnestrovian Moldavian Soviet Socialist Republic</a> (PMSSR) was proclaimed as a Soviet republic by an <i><a href="/wiki/Ad_hoc" title="Ad hoc">ad hoc</a></i> assembly, the Second Congress of the Peoples' Representatives of Transnistria, following a <a href="/wiki/1989%E2%80%931990_Transnistrian_referendum" title="1989–1990 Transnistrian referendum">successful referendum</a>. Violence escalated when in October 1990 the Popular Front called for volunteers to form armed militias to stop an autonomy referendum in <a href="/wiki/Gagauzia" title="Gagauzia">Gagauzia</a>, which had an even higher share of ethnic minorities. In response, volunteer militias were formed in Transnistria. In April 1990, nationalist mobs attacked ethnic Russian members of parliament, while the Moldovan police refused to intervene or restore order.<sup id="cite_ref-Kaufman143_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kaufman143-42">[41]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In the interest of preserving a unified Moldavian SSR within the USSR and preventing the situation escalating further, then <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="President of the Soviet Union">Soviet President</a> Mikhail Gorbachev, while citing the restriction of civil rights of ethnic minorities by Moldova as the cause of the dispute, declared the Transnistria proclamation to be lacking legal basis and annulled it by presidential decree on 22 December 1990.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[42]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[43]</a></sup> Nevertheless, no significant action was taken against Transnistria and the new authorities were slowly able to establish control of the region. </p>
      <p>Following the <a href="/wiki/1991_Soviet_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat_attempt" title="1991 Soviet coup d'état attempt">1991 Soviet coup d'état attempt</a>, the Pridnestrovian Moldavian SSR declared its independence from the Soviet Union; on 5 November 1991 Transnistria abandoned its socialist ideology and was renamed "Priednestrovian Moldavian Republic".<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[44]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transnistria_War">Transnistria War</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Transnistria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Transnistria War">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transnistria_War" title="Transnistria War">Transnistria War</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The Transnistria War followed armed clashes on a limited scale that broke out between Transnistrian separatists and Moldova as early as November 1990 at <a href="/wiki/Dub%C4%83sari" title="Dubăsari">Dubăsari</a>. Volunteers, including <a href="/wiki/Cossacks" title="Cossacks">Cossacks</a>, came from Russia to help the separatist side.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[45]</a></sup> In mid-April 1992, under the agreements on the split of the military equipment of the former Soviet Union negotiated between the former 15 republics in the previous months, Moldova created its own Defence Ministry. According to the decree of its creation, most of the 14th Soviet Army's military equipment was to be retained by Moldova.<sup id="cite_ref-Bergman_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bergman-47">[46]</a></sup> Starting from 2 March 1992, there was concerted military action between Moldova and Transnistria. The fighting intensified throughout early 1992. The former Soviet 14th Guards Army entered the conflict in its final stage, opening fire against Moldovan forces;<sup id="cite_ref-Bergman_47-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bergman-47">[46]</a></sup> approximately 700 people were killed. Moldova has since then exercised no effective control or influence on Transnistrian authorities. A ceasefire agreement, signed on 21 July 1992, has held to the present day. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Further_negotiations">Further negotiations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Transnistria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Further negotiations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Dmitry_Medvedev_18_March_2009-2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Dmitry_Medvedev_18_March_2009-2.jpg/220px-Dmitry_Medvedev_18_March_2009-2.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Dmitry_Medvedev_18_March_2009-2.jpg/330px-Dmitry_Medvedev_18_March_2009-2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Dmitry_Medvedev_18_March_2009-2.jpg/440px-Dmitry_Medvedev_18_March_2009-2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="334"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Dmitry_Medvedev_18_March_2009-2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Igor_Smirnov" title="Igor Smirnov">Igor Smirnov</a> with <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Voronin" title="Vladimir Voronin">Vladimir Voronin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dmitry_Medvedev" title="Dmitry Medvedev">Dmitry Medvedev</a> in <a href="/wiki/Barvikha" title="Barvikha">Barvikha</a>, 18 March 2009
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Organization_for_Security_and_Co-operation_in_Europe" title="Organization for Security and Co-operation in Europe">Organization for Security and Co-operation in Europe</a> (OSCE) is trying to facilitate a negotiated settlement. Under OSCE auspices, on 8 May 1997, Moldovan President <a href="/wiki/Petru_Lucinschi" title="Petru Lucinschi">Petru Lucinschi</a> and Transnistrian president <a href="/wiki/Igor_Smirnov" title="Igor Smirnov">Igor Smirnov</a>, signed the "Memorandum on the principles of normalization of the relations between the Republic of Moldova and Transnistria", also known as the "Primakov Memorandum", sustaining the establishment of legal and state relations, although the memorandum's provisions were interpreted differently by the governments of Moldova and Transnistria. </p>
      <p>In November 2003, <a href="/wiki/Dmitry_Kozak" title="Dmitry Kozak">Dmitry Kozak</a>, a counselor of Russian president <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Putin" title="Vladimir Putin">Vladimir Putin</a>, proposed a memorandum on the creation of an <a href="/wiki/Asymmetric_federalism" title="Asymmetric federalism">asymmetric</a> federal Moldovan state, with Moldova holding a majority and Transnistria being a minority part of the federation.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[47]</a></sup> Known as "the <a href="/wiki/Kozak_memorandum" title="Kozak memorandum">Kozak memorandum</a>", it did not coincide with the Transnistrian position, which sought equal status between Transnistria and Moldova, but gave Transnistria veto powers over future constitutional changes; this encouraged Transnistria to sign it. Moldovan President <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Voronin" title="Vladimir Voronin">Vladimir Voronin</a> was initially supportive of the plan, but refused to sign it after internal opposition and international pressure from the OSCE and US, and after Russia had endorsed the Transnistrian demand to maintain a Russian military presence for the next 20 years as a guarantee for the intended federation.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[48]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Talks were started in 2006 to deal with the problems, but without results for many years. In February 2011 the so-called "<span class="nowrap">5 + 2</span> Talks" (thus named because they were carried out by Transnistria, Moldova, Ukraine, Russia and the OSCE, plus the US and the EU as external observers) were started again in <a href="/wiki/Vienna" title="Vienna">Vienna</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[49]</a></sup> After the annexation of the Crimea by Russia in March 2014, the head of the Transnistrian parliament asked to join the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Federation" class="mw-redirect" title="Russian Federation">Russian Federation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[50]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[51]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[52]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Transnistria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Disputed_status_of_Transnistria#Territorial_issues" class="mw-redirect" title="Disputed status of Transnistria">Disputed status of Transnistria: Territorial issues</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_places_in_Transnistria" class="mw-redirect" title="List of places in Transnistria">List of places in Transnistria</a>
      </div>

       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Naddniestrze.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Naddniestrze.png/220px-Naddniestrze.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="314" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Naddniestrze.png/330px-Naddniestrze.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Naddniestrze.png/440px-Naddniestrze.png 2x" data-file-width="2655" data-file-height="3786"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Naddniestrze.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>General map of Transnistria
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Dniester_in_Bender_01.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Dniester_in_Bender_01.JPG/220px-Dniester_in_Bender_01.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Dniester_in_Bender_01.JPG/330px-Dniester_in_Bender_01.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Dniester_in_Bender_01.JPG/440px-Dniester_in_Bender_01.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3200" data-file-height="2400"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Dniester_in_Bender_01.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Dniester_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Dniester River">Dniester River</a> in <a href="/wiki/Bender,_Moldova" title="Bender, Moldova">Bender</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Transnistria is <a href="/wiki/Landlocked" class="mw-redirect" title="Landlocked">landlocked</a> and borders <a href="/wiki/Bessarabia" title="Bessarabia">Bessarabia</a> (i.e., the rest of Moldova, for 411&nbsp;km, 255 miles) to the west, and <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukraine</a> (for 405&nbsp;km, 250 miles) to the east. It is a narrow valley stretching north–south along the bank of the <a href="/wiki/Dniester_river" class="mw-redirect" title="Dniester river">Dniester river</a>, which forms a natural boundary along most of the border with (the rest of) Moldova. </p>
      <p>The territory controlled by the PMR is mostly, but not completely, coincident with the left (eastern) bank of Dniester. It includes ten cities and towns, and 69 communes, with a total of 147 localities (counting the unincorporated ones as well). Six communes on the left bank (<a href="/wiki/Cocieri" title="Cocieri">Cocieri</a>, <a href="/wiki/Molovata_Nou%C4%83" title="Molovata Nouă">Molovata Nouă</a>, <a href="/wiki/Corjova,_Dub%C4%83sari" title="Corjova, Dubăsari">Corjova</a>, <a href="/wiki/P%C3%AEr%C3%AEta" title="Pîrîta">Pîrîta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Co%C8%99ni%C8%9Ba" title="Coșnița">Coșnița</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Doro%C8%9Bcaia" title="Doroțcaia">Doroțcaia</a>) remained under the control of the Moldovan government after the War of Transnistria in 1992, as part of the <a href="/wiki/Dub%C4%83sari_District" title="Dubăsari District">Dubăsari District</a>. They are situated north and south of the city of <a href="/wiki/Dub%C4%83sari" title="Dubăsari">Dubăsari</a>, which itself is under PMR control. The village of Roghi of Molovata Nouă Commune is also controlled by the PMR (Moldova controls the other nine of the ten villages of the six communes). </p>
      <p>On the west bank, in Bessarabia, the city of <a href="/wiki/Bender,_Moldova" title="Bender, Moldova">Bender</a> and four communes (containing six villages) to its east, south-east, and south, on the opposite bank of the river Dniester from the city of Tiraspol (<a href="/wiki/Proteagailovca" title="Proteagailovca">Proteagailovca</a>, <a href="/wiki/G%C3%AEsca" title="Gîsca">Gîsca</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chi%C8%9Bcani,_Moldova" class="mw-redirect" title="Chițcani, Moldova">Chițcani</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Cremenciug,_C%C4%83u%C8%99eni" title="Cremenciug, Căușeni">Cremenciug</a>) are controlled by the PMR. </p>
      <p>The localities controlled by Moldova on the eastern bank, the village of <a href="/wiki/Roghi" class="mw-redirect" title="Roghi">Roghi</a>, and the city of Dubăsari (situated on the eastern bank and controlled by the PMR) form a security zone along with the six villages and one city controlled by the PMR on the western bank, as well as two (<a href="/wiki/Varni%C8%9Ba,_Anenii_Noi" title="Varnița, Anenii Noi">Varnița</a> and <a href="/wiki/Copanca" title="Copanca">Copanca</a>) on the same west bank under Moldovan control. The security situation inside it is subject to the <a href="/wiki/Joint_Control_Commission" title="Joint Control Commission">Joint Control Commission</a> rulings. </p>
      <p>The main transportation route in Transnistria is the road from Tiraspol to Rîbnița through Dubăsari. North and south of Dubăsari it passes through the lands of the villages controlled by Moldova (<a href="/wiki/Doro%C8%9Bcaia" title="Doroțcaia">Doroțcaia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cocieri" title="Cocieri">Cocieri</a>, <a href="/wiki/Roghi" class="mw-redirect" title="Roghi">Roghi</a>, while <a href="/wiki/Sovetscoe" title="Sovetscoe">Vasilievca</a> is entirely situated east of the road). Conflict erupted on several occasions when the PMR prevented the villagers from reaching their farmland east of the road.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[53]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[54]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[55]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Transnistrians are able to travel (normally without difficulty) in and out of the territory under PMR control to neighbouring Moldovan-controlled territory, to Ukraine, and on to Russia, by road or (when service is not interrupted by political tensions) on two international trains, the year-round Moscow-Chișinău, and the seasonal <a href="/wiki/Saratov" title="Saratov">Saratov</a>-<a href="/wiki/Varna,_Bulgaria" title="Varna, Bulgaria">Varna</a>. International air travellers rely on the airport in <a href="/wiki/Chi%C8%99in%C4%83u" title="Chișinău">Chișinău</a>, the Moldovan capital, or the airport in <a href="/wiki/Odessa" title="Odessa">Odessa</a>, in Ukraine. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Transnistria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Administrative divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Pridnestrian_Administration.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Pridnestrian_Administration.png/170px-Pridnestrian_Administration.png" decoding="async" width="170" height="250" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Pridnestrian_Administration.png/255px-Pridnestrian_Administration.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Pridnestrian_Administration.png/340px-Pridnestrian_Administration.png 2x" data-file-width="922" data-file-height="1354"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Pridnestrian_Administration.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Districts of Transnistria
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Transnistria is subdivided into five districts (<i><a href="/wiki/Raion" title="Raion">raions</a></i>) and one municipality, the City of Tiraspol (which is entirely surrounded by but administratively distinct from Slobozia District), listed below from north to south (Russian names and <a href="/wiki/Transliteration" title="Transliteration">transliterations</a> are appended in parentheses). In addition, another municipality, the City of Bender, situated on the western bank of the Dniester, in Bessarabia, and geographically outside Transnistria, is not part of the territorial unit of Transnistria as defined by the Moldovan central authorities, but it is controlled by the PMR authorities, which consider it part of PMR's administrative organisation: </p>

      <p>Each of the districts is further divided into cities and communes. </p>
