      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Political_status">Political status</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Transnistria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Political status">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Political_status_of_Transnistria" title="Political status of Transnistria">Political status of Transnistria</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Transnistria_in_Moldova_(de-facto)_(semi-secession).svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Transnistria_in_Moldova_%28de-facto%29_%28semi-secession%29.svg/220px-Transnistria_in_Moldova_%28de-facto%29_%28semi-secession%29.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="270" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Transnistria_in_Moldova_%28de-facto%29_%28semi-secession%29.svg/330px-Transnistria_in_Moldova_%28de-facto%29_%28semi-secession%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Transnistria_in_Moldova_%28de-facto%29_%28semi-secession%29.svg/440px-Transnistria_in_Moldova_%28de-facto%29_%28semi-secession%29.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="990" data-file-height="1217"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Transnistria_in_Moldova_(de-facto)_(semi-secession).svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Transnistrian territory in relation to the rest of <a href="/wiki/Moldova" title="Moldova">Moldova</a>, <a href="/wiki/Landlocked_country" title="Landlocked country">landlocked</a> along the border with <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukraine</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Transnistria_dup%C4%83_Asybaris.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Transnistria_dup%C4%83_Asybaris.jpg/220px-Transnistria_dup%C4%83_Asybaris.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="324" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Transnistria_dup%C4%83_Asybaris.jpg/330px-Transnistria_dup%C4%83_Asybaris.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Transnistria_dup%C4%83_Asybaris.jpg/440px-Transnistria_dup%C4%83_Asybaris.jpg 2x" data-file-width="978" data-file-height="1442"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Transnistria_dup%C4%83_Asybaris.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Political map of Transnistria with the differences between the <i><a href="/wiki/De_facto" title="De facto">de facto</a></i> Pridnestrovian Moldavian Republic and the <i><a href="/wiki/De_jure" title="De jure">de jure</a></i> Autonomous Dniestrian Territory
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>All UN member states consider Transnistria a legal part of the Republic of <a href="/wiki/Moldova" title="Moldova">Moldova</a>. Only the <a href="/wiki/List_of_states_with_limited_recognition" title="List of states with limited recognition">partially recognised states</a> of <a href="/wiki/South_Ossetia" title="South Ossetia">South Ossetia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Artsakh" title="Republic of Artsakh">Artsakh</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Abkhazia" title="Abkhazia">Abkhazia</a> have recognised Transnistria as a sovereign entity after it declared independence from Moldova in 1990 with <a href="/wiki/Tiraspol" title="Tiraspol">Tiraspol</a> as its declared capital. </p>
      <p>Between 1929 and 1940, Tiraspol functioned as the capital of the <a href="/wiki/Moldavian_Autonomous_Soviet_Socialist_Republic" title="Moldavian Autonomous Soviet Socialist Republic">Moldavian ASSR</a>, an autonomous republic that existed from 1924 to 1940 within the <a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_SSR" class="mw-redirect" title="Ukrainian SSR">Ukrainian SSR</a>. </p>
      <p>Although exercising no direct control over the territory of Transnistria, the Moldovan government passed the "Law on Basic Provisions of the Special Legal Status of Localities from the Left Bank of the Dniester" on 22 July 2005, which established part of Transnistria (territory of Pridnestrovian Moldavian Republic without Bender and without territories, which are under control of Moldova) as an <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_territorial_unit_with_special_legal_status_Transnistria" class="mw-redirect" title="Autonomous territorial unit with special legal status Transnistria">autonomous territorial unit</a> within the Republic of Moldova. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:%D0%92%D1%81%D1%82%D1%80%D0%B5%D1%87%D0%B0_%D0%9F%D0%B0%D1%82%D1%80%D0%B8%D0%B0%D1%80%D1%85%D0%B0_%D0%9A%D0%B8%D1%80%D0%B8%D0%BB%D0%BB%D0%B0_%D0%B2_%D0%9F%D1%80%D0%B8%D0%B4%D0%BD%D0%B5%D1%81%D1%82%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%B2%D1%8C%D0%B5.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/%D0%92%D1%81%D1%82%D1%80%D0%B5%D1%87%D0%B0_%D0%9F%D0%B0%D1%82%D1%80%D0%B8%D0%B0%D1%80%D1%85%D0%B0_%D0%9A%D0%B8%D1%80%D0%B8%D0%BB%D0%BB%D0%B0_%D0%B2_%D0%9F%D1%80%D0%B8%D0%B4%D0%BD%D0%B5%D1%81%D1%82%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%B2%D1%8C%D0%B5.jpg/220px-%D0%92%D1%81%D1%82%D1%80%D0%B5%D1%87%D0%B0_%D0%9F%D0%B0%D1%82%D1%80%D0%B8%D0%B0%D1%80%D1%85%D0%B0_%D0%9A%D0%B8%D1%80%D0%B8%D0%BB%D0%BB%D0%B0_%D0%B2_%D0%9F%D1%80%D0%B8%D0%B4%D0%BD%D0%B5%D1%81%D1%82%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%B2%D1%8C%D0%B5.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/%D0%92%D1%81%D1%82%D1%80%D0%B5%D1%87%D0%B0_%D0%9F%D0%B0%D1%82%D1%80%D0%B8%D0%B0%D1%80%D1%85%D0%B0_%D0%9A%D0%B8%D1%80%D0%B8%D0%BB%D0%BB%D0%B0_%D0%B2_%D0%9F%D1%80%D0%B8%D0%B4%D0%BD%D0%B5%D1%81%D1%82%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%B2%D1%8C%D0%B5.jpg/330px-%D0%92%D1%81%D1%82%D1%80%D0%B5%D1%87%D0%B0_%D0%9F%D0%B0%D1%82%D1%80%D0%B8%D0%B0%D1%80%D1%85%D0%B0_%D0%9A%D0%B8%D1%80%D0%B8%D0%BB%D0%BB%D0%B0_%D0%B2_%D0%9F%D1%80%D0%B8%D0%B4%D0%BD%D0%B5%D1%81%D1%82%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%B2%D1%8C%D0%B5.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/%D0%92%D1%81%D1%82%D1%80%D0%B5%D1%87%D0%B0_%D0%9F%D0%B0%D1%82%D1%80%D0%B8%D0%B0%D1%80%D1%85%D0%B0_%D0%9A%D0%B8%D1%80%D0%B8%D0%BB%D0%BB%D0%B0_%D0%B2_%D0%9F%D1%80%D0%B8%D0%B4%D0%BD%D0%B5%D1%81%D1%82%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%B2%D1%8C%D0%B5.jpg/440px-%D0%92%D1%81%D1%82%D1%80%D0%B5%D1%87%D0%B0_%D0%9F%D0%B0%D1%82%D1%80%D0%B8%D0%B0%D1%80%D1%85%D0%B0_%D0%9A%D0%B8%D1%80%D0%B8%D0%BB%D0%BB%D0%B0_%D0%B2_%D0%9F%D1%80%D0%B8%D0%B4%D0%BD%D0%B5%D1%81%D1%82%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%B2%D1%8C%D0%B5.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="667"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:%D0%92%D1%81%D1%82%D1%80%D0%B5%D1%87%D0%B0_%D0%9F%D0%B0%D1%82%D1%80%D0%B8%D0%B0%D1%80%D1%85%D0%B0_%D0%9A%D0%B8%D1%80%D0%B8%D0%BB%D0%BB%D0%B0_%D0%B2_%D0%9F%D1%80%D0%B8%D0%B4%D0%BD%D0%B5%D1%81%D1%82%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%B2%D1%8C%D0%B5.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Former <a href="/wiki/President_of_Transnistria" title="President of Transnistria">President of Transnistria</a> <a href="/wiki/Yevgeny_Shevchuk" title="Yevgeny Shevchuk">Yevgeny Shevchuk</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sabbas_(Volkov)" title="Sabbas (Volkov)">Sabbas</a>, diocesan bishop of the <a href="/wiki/Moldovan_Orthodox_Church" class="mw-redirect" title="Moldovan Orthodox Church">Moldovan Orthodox Church</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>As of 2009<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Transnistria&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> the population of Transnistria comprised about 555,000 people. Ninety percent of the population of Transnistria are citizens of Transnistria.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[56]</a></sup> Transnistrians have dual or triple citizenship, including: </p> 
      <ul>
       <li>Citizens of Moldova<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[57]</a></sup> – around 300,000 people (including dual citizens of Moldova and Russia (around 20,000<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[58]</a></sup>) or of Moldova and the EU states (around 80%) of Romania,<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[59]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[60]</a></sup> Bulgaria, or the Czech Republic)</li> 
       <li>Citizens of Russia – around 150,000 people (including around 15,000 dual citizens of Belarus, Israel, Turkey); excluding those holding dual citizenship of Russia and of Moldova (around 20,000)</li> 
       <li>Citizens of Ukraine – around 100,000 people<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[61]</a></sup> There are around 20,000–30,000 people with dual citizenship (Moldova and Ukraine, or Russia and Ukraine) or triple citizenship (Moldova, Russia and Ukraine). They are included in the number of Ukrainian citizens.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[62]</a></sup></li> 
       <li>Persons without citizenship – around 20,000–30,000 people</li>
      </ul> 
      <p>There are unsettled <a href="/wiki/Disputed_status_of_Transnistria" class="mw-redirect" title="Disputed status of Transnistria">border issues</a> between Transnistria and Moldova. Fifteen villages from the eleven communes of <a href="/wiki/Dub%C4%83sari_District" title="Dubăsari District">Dubăsari District</a>, including <a href="/wiki/Cocieri" title="Cocieri">Cocieri</a> and <a href="/wiki/Doro%C8%9Bcaia" title="Doroțcaia">Doroțcaia</a> that geographically belong to Transnistria, have been under the control of the central government of Moldova after the involvement of local inhabitants on the side of Moldovan forces during the War of Transnistria. These villages, along with <a href="/wiki/Varni%C8%9Ba,_Anenii_Noi" title="Varnița, Anenii Noi">Varnița</a> and <a href="/wiki/Copanca" title="Copanca">Copanca</a>, near Bender and Tiraspol, are claimed by the PMR. One city (Bender) and six villages on the west bank are controlled by the PMR, but are considered by Moldova as a separate municipality (Bender and village of <a href="/wiki/Proteagailovca" title="Proteagailovca">Proteagailovca</a>) or part of the <a href="/wiki/C%C4%83u%C8%99eni_District" title="Căușeni District">Căușeni District</a> (five villages in three communes). </p>
      <p>Tense situations have periodically surfaced due to these territorial disputes, such as in 2005, when Transnistrian forces entered Vasilievca,<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[63]</a></sup> in 2006 around Varnița, and in 2007 in the Dubăsari-Cocieri area, when a confrontation between Moldovan and Transnistrian forces occurred, however without any casualties. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="International_relations">International relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Transnistria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: International relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/International_recognition_of_Transnistria" title="International recognition of Transnistria">International recognition of Transnistria</a> and <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Transnistria" title="Foreign relations of Transnistria">Foreign relations of Transnistria</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Transnistria.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Transnistria.jpg/170px-Transnistria.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="230" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Transnistria.jpg/255px-Transnistria.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Transnistria.jpg/340px-Transnistria.jpg 2x" data-file-width="758" data-file-height="1024"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Transnistria.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A <a href="/wiki/Transnistrian_passport" title="Transnistrian passport">Transnistrian passport</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Nina_Shtanski" title="Nina Shtanski">Nina Shtanski</a> served as Transnistria's Minister of Foreign Affairs from 2012 to 2015; <a href="/w/index.php?title=Vitaly_Ignatiev&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Vitaly Ignatiev (page does not exist)">Vitaly Ignatiev</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">&nbsp;[<a href="https://ru.wikipedia.org/wiki/%D0%98%D0%B3%D0%BD%D0%B0%D1%82%D1%8C%D0%B5%D0%B2,_%D0%92%D0%B8%D1%82%D0%B0%D0%BB%D0%B8%D0%B9_%D0%92%D0%B8%D0%BA%D1%82%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B8%D1%87" class="extiw" title="ru:Игнатьев, Виталий Викторович">ru</a>]</span> succeeded her as minister. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government_and_politics">Government and politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Transnistria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Government and politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Transnistria" title="Politics of Transnistria">Politics of Transnistria</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Government_building_Tiraspol_02.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Government_building_Tiraspol_02.jpg/220px-Government_building_Tiraspol_02.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Government_building_Tiraspol_02.jpg/330px-Government_building_Tiraspol_02.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/2/2a/Government_building_Tiraspol_02.jpg 2x" data-file-width="400" data-file-height="300"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Government_building_Tiraspol_02.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The Transnistrian parliament building in <a href="/wiki/Tiraspol" title="Tiraspol">Tiraspol</a>, fronted by a statue of <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin" title="Vladimir Lenin">Vladimir Lenin</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Transnistria is a <a href="/wiki/Presidential_system" title="Presidential system">presidential</a> <a href="/wiki/Democracy" title="Democracy">democracy</a>. The president is directly elected for a maximum of two consecutive five-year terms. The current President is <a href="/wiki/Vadim_Krasnoselsky" title="Vadim Krasnoselsky">Vadim Krasnoselsky</a>. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_Transnistria" class="mw-redirect" title="Parliament of Transnistria">Supreme Council</a> is a unicameral legislature. It has 43 members who are elected for 5-year terms. Elections take place within a <a href="/wiki/Multi-party_system" title="Multi-party system">multi-party system</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[64]</a></sup> The majority in the Parliament of Transnistria belongs to the <a href="/wiki/Renewal_(Transnistria)" class="mw-redirect" title="Renewal (Transnistria)">Renewal</a> movement that defeated the <a href="/wiki/Republic_(Transnistria)" title="Republic (Transnistria)">Republic</a> party affiliated with Igor Smirnov in 2005 and performed even better in the <a href="/wiki/2010_Transnistrian_legislative_election" class="mw-redirect" title="2010 Transnistrian legislative election">2010</a> and <a href="/wiki/2015_Transnistrian_legislative_election" class="mw-redirect" title="2015 Transnistrian legislative election">2015</a> elections. Elections in Transnistria are not recognised by international bodies such as the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>, as well as numerous individual countries, who called them a source of increased tensions. </p>
      <p>There is disagreement over whether <a href="/wiki/Elections_in_Transnistria" class="mw-redirect" title="Elections in Transnistria">elections in Transnistria</a> are free and fair. The political regime has been described as one of "super-<a href="/wiki/Presidentialism" class="mw-redirect" title="Presidentialism">presidentialism</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-Herd_05_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Herd_05-66">[65]</a></sup> During the 2006 presidential election, the registration of opposition candidate <a href="/wiki/Andrey_Safonov" class="mw-redirect" title="Andrey Safonov">Andrey Safonov</a> was delayed until a few days before the vote, so that he had little time to conduct an election campaign.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[66]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[67]</a></sup> Some sources consider election results suspect. In 2001, in one region it was reported that <a href="/wiki/Igor_Smirnov" title="Igor Smirnov">Igor Smirnov</a> collected 103.6% of the votes.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[68]</a></sup> The PMR government said "the government of Moldova launched a campaign aimed at convincing international observers not to attend" an election held on 11 December 2005—but CIS election monitors had ignored that and had declared the ballot democratic. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:%D0%94%D0%BE%D0%BC_%D0%A1%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B5%D1%82%D0%BE%D0%B2_2006.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/%D0%94%D0%BE%D0%BC_%D0%A1%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B5%D1%82%D0%BE%D0%B2_2006.jpg/220px-%D0%94%D0%BE%D0%BC_%D0%A1%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B5%D1%82%D0%BE%D0%B2_2006.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/%D0%94%D0%BE%D0%BC_%D0%A1%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B5%D1%82%D0%BE%D0%B2_2006.jpg/330px-%D0%94%D0%BE%D0%BC_%D0%A1%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B5%D1%82%D0%BE%D0%B2_2006.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/c/cf/%D0%94%D0%BE%D0%BC_%D0%A1%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B5%D1%82%D0%BE%D0%B2_2006.jpg 2x" data-file-width="400" data-file-height="300"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:%D0%94%D0%BE%D0%BC_%D0%A1%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B5%D1%82%D0%BE%D0%B2_2006.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Tiraspol" title="Tiraspol">Tiraspol</a> City Council
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The opposition <a href="/wiki/Power_to_the_People_(political_party)" title="Power to the People (political party)">Narodovlastie party</a> and Power to the People movement were outlawed at the beginning of 2000<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[69]</a></sup> and eventually dissolved.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[70]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[71]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>A list published by the European Union bans travel to the EU for some members of the Transnistrian leadership.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[72]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2007, the registration of a Social Democratic Party was allowed. This party, led by former separatist leader and member of the PMR government <a href="/wiki/Andrey_Safonov" class="mw-redirect" title="Andrey Safonov">Andrey Safonov</a>, allegedly favours a union with Moldova. </p>
      <p>In September 2007, the leader of the Transnistrian Communist Party, <a href="/wiki/Oleg_Horjan" class="mw-redirect" title="Oleg Horjan">Oleg Horjan</a>, was sentenced to a suspended sentence of 1½ years' imprisonment for organising unsanctioned actions of protest.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[73]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>According to the <a href="/wiki/2006_Transnistrian_independence_referendum" title="2006 Transnistrian independence referendum">2006 referendum</a>, carried out by the PMR government, 97.2% of the population voted in favour of "independence from Moldova and free association with Russia".<sup id="cite_ref-msca_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-msca-75">[74]</a></sup> EU and several other countries refused to recognise the referendum results. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transnistria_border_customs_dispute">Transnistria border customs dispute</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Transnistria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Transnistria border customs dispute">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transnistria_border_customs_issue" class="mw-redirect" title="Transnistria border customs issue">Transnistria border customs issue</a>
      </div> 
      <p>On 3 March 2006, <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukraine</a> introduced new customs regulations on its border with Transnistria. Ukraine declared that it would import goods from Transnistria only with documents processed by Moldovan <a href="/wiki/Customs" title="Customs">customs</a> offices as part of the implementation of the joint customs protocol agreed between Ukraine and Moldova on 30 December 2005. Transnistria and Russia termed the act an "economic blockade". </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>, the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Organization_for_Security_and_Co-operation_in_Europe" title="Organization for Security and Co-operation in Europe">OSCE</a> approved the Ukrainian move, while Russia saw it as a means of political pressure. On 4 March, Transnistria responded by blocking the Moldovan and Ukrainian transport at the borders of Transnistria. The Transnistrian block was lifted after two weeks. However, the Moldovan/Ukrainian block remains in place and holds up progress in status settlement negotiations between the sides.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[75]</a></sup> In the months after the regulations, exports from Transnistria declined drastically. Transnistria declared a "humanitarian catastrophe" in the region, while Moldova called the declaration "deliberate misinformation".<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[76]</a></sup> Cargoes of humanitarian aid were sent from Russia in response. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Tiraspol_(11377750435).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Tiraspol_%2811377750435%29.jpg/220px-Tiraspol_%2811377750435%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Tiraspol_%2811377750435%29.jpg/330px-Tiraspol_%2811377750435%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Tiraspol_%2811377750435%29.jpg/440px-Tiraspol_%2811377750435%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Tiraspol_(11377750435).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>World War II-era Soviet <a href="/wiki/T-34" title="T-34">T-34</a> in Tiraspol
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Russian_military_presence_in_Transnistria">Russian military presence in Transnistria</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Transnistria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Russian military presence in Transnistria">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/14th_Army_involvement_in_Transnistria" title="14th Army involvement in Transnistria">14th Army involvement in Transnistria</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The 1992 cease-fire agreement between Moldova and Transnistria established a Russian peace-keeper presence in Transnistria and a 1,200-member Russian military contingent is present in Transnistria. Russian troops stationed in parts of Moldova except Transnistria since the time of the USSR were fully withdrawn to Russia by January 1993. </p>
      <p>In April 1995, the Soviet 14th Guards Army became the <a href="/wiki/Operational_Group_of_Russian_Forces" title="Operational Group of Russian Forces">Operational Group of Russian Forces</a>, which by the 2010s had shrunk to two battalions and no more than 1,500 troops. </p>
      <p>On 21 October 1994, Russia and Moldova signed an agreement that committed Russia to the withdrawal of the troops in three years from the date of entry into force of the agreement;<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[77]</a></sup> this did not come into effect, however, because the Russian <a href="/wiki/State_Duma" title="State Duma">Duma</a> did not ratify it.<sup id="cite_ref-DFSTATES_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DFSTATES-17">[16]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Treaty_on_Conventional_Armed_Forces_in_Europe" title="Treaty on Conventional Armed Forces in Europe">Treaty on Conventional Armed Forces in Europe</a> (CFE) included a paragraph about the removal of Russian troops from Moldova's territory and was introduced into the text of the OSCE Summit Declaration of <a href="/wiki/Istanbul" title="Istanbul">Istanbul</a> (1999) in which Russia had committed itself to pulling out its troops from Transnistria by the end of 2002.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[78]</a></sup> However, even after 2002, the Russian parliament did not ratify the Istanbul accords. On 19 July 2004, after it finally passed through parliament President <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Putin" title="Vladimir Putin">Vladimir Putin</a> signed the Law on the ratification of the CFE Treaty in Europe, which committed Russia to remove the heavy armaments limited by this Treaty.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[79]</a></sup> During 2000–2001, although the CFE Treaty was not fully ratified, to comply with it, Moscow withdrew 125 pieces of Treaty Limited Equipment (TLE) and 60 railway wagons containing ammunition from the Transnistrian region of Moldova. In 2002, Russia withdrew three trainloads (118 railway wagons) of military equipment and two (43 wagons) of ammunition from the Transnistrian region of Moldova, and in 2003, 11 rail convoys transporting military equipment and 31 transporting ammunition. According to the <a href="/wiki/OSCE" class="mw-redirect" title="OSCE">OSCE</a> Mission to Moldova, of a total of 42,000 tons of ammunition stored in Transnistria, 1,153 tons (3%) was transported back to Russia in 2001, 2,405 tons (6%) in 2002 and 16,573 tons (39%) in 2003.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Andrei_Stratan" title="Andrei Stratan">Andrei Stratan</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Minister_of_Foreign_Affairs_of_Moldova" class="mw-redirect" title="Minister of Foreign Affairs of Moldova">Minister of Foreign Affairs of Moldova</a>, stated in his speech during the 12th OSCE Ministerial Council Meeting in <a href="/wiki/Sofia" title="Sofia">Sofia</a> on 6–7 December 2004 that "The presence of Russian troops on the territory of the Republic of Moldova is against the political will of Moldovan constitutional authorities and defies the unanimously recognized international norms and principles, being qualified by Moldovan authorities as a foreign military occupation illegally deployed on the territory of the state".<sup id="cite_ref-gribincea_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gribincea-81">[80]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[81]</a></sup> As of 2007<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Transnistria&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> however, Russia insists that it has already fulfilled those obligations. It states the remaining troops are serving as peacekeepers authorised under the 1992 ceasefire, are not in violation of the Istanbul accords and will remain until the conflict is fully resolved.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[82]</a></sup> On the other hand, Moldova believes that fewer than 500 soldiers are authorised pursuant to the ceasefire and, in 2015, began to arrest and deport Russian soldiers who are part of the excess forces and attempt to use Moldovan airports.<sup id="cite_ref-EurasiaNet_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EurasiaNet-84">[83]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Russian_Peace_Keeping_soldiers_(14934029697).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Russian_Peace_Keeping_soldiers_%2814934029697%29.jpg/220px-Russian_Peace_Keeping_soldiers_%2814934029697%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Russian_Peace_Keeping_soldiers_%2814934029697%29.jpg/330px-Russian_Peace_Keeping_soldiers_%2814934029697%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Russian_Peace_Keeping_soldiers_%2814934029697%29.jpg/440px-Russian_Peace_Keeping_soldiers_%2814934029697%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4608" data-file-height="3456"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Russian_Peace_Keeping_soldiers_(14934029697).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Joint_Control_Commission" title="Joint Control Commission">Russian peace-keeping</a> soldiers at the border between Transnistria and Moldova at <a href="/wiki/Dub%C4%83sari" title="Dubăsari">Dubăsari</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In a <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a> resolution on 18 November 2008, Russia was urged to withdraw its military presence from the "Transdnestrian region of Moldova".<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[84]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2011, US Senator <a href="/wiki/John_McCain" title="John McCain">John McCain</a> claimed in a visit to Moldova that Moscow is violating the territorial integrity of Moldova and Georgia and one of the "fundamental norms" of "international behavior".<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[85]</a></sup> On 21 May 2015, the <a href="/wiki/Verkhovna_Rada" title="Verkhovna Rada">Ukrainian parliament</a> passed a law terminating five co-operation agreements with Russia. This law effectively terminates the "Agreement on transit of Russian military units temporarily located on the territory of the Republic of Moldova through the territory of Ukraine" dated 4 December 1998.<sup id="cite_ref-EurasiaNet_84-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EurasiaNet-84">[83]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[86]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>One point of access for Russian soldiers travelling to Transnistria remains <a href="/wiki/Chi%C8%99in%C4%83u_International_Airport" title="Chișinău International Airport">Chișinău International Airport</a> and the short overland journey from there to Tiraspol. Over the years, Moldova has largely permitted Russian officers and soldiers to transit the airport on their way to Transnistria, though at some points (for example in 2015), Chișinău has periodically blocked and deported soldiers who were not clearly identified as international peacekeepers or who have failed to give sufficient advance notice. Chișinău would likely only ever agree to the possibility of moving employees, officers, and soldiers of the peacekeeping forces. The passage of soldiers of the <a href="/wiki/14th_Army_involvement_in_Transnistria" title="14th Army involvement in Transnistria">14th Army</a> would be illegal.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[87]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On 27 June 2016, a new law entered in force in Transnistria, punishing actions or public statements, including through the usage of mass media, networks of information and telecommunications or the Internet, criticizing the peace-keeping mission of the Russian Army in the Transnistrian Moldovan Republic, or presenting interpretations perceived to be "false" by the Transnistrian government of the Russian Army's peacekeeping mission. The punishment is up to three years of jail for ordinary people or up to seven years of jail if the crime was committed by a person of responsibility or a group of persons by prior agreement.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[88]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint noexcerpt Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:NOTRS" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:NOTRS"><span title="This claim needs references to better sources. (April 2017)">better&nbsp;source&nbsp;needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Transnistria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Military">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Military_of_Transnistria" class="mw-redirect" title="Military of Transnistria">Military of Transnistria</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:TIraspol_Transnistria_(13954559507).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/TIraspol_Transnistria_%2813954559507%29.jpg/220px-TIraspol_Transnistria_%2813954559507%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/TIraspol_Transnistria_%2813954559507%29.jpg/330px-TIraspol_Transnistria_%2813954559507%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/TIraspol_Transnistria_%2813954559507%29.jpg/440px-TIraspol_Transnistria_%2813954559507%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4608" data-file-height="3456"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:TIraspol_Transnistria_(13954559507).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Transnistrian soldiers in 2013
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>As of 2007<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Transnistria&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the <a href="/wiki/Armed_Forces_of_Transnistria" title="Armed Forces of Transnistria">armed forces and the paramilitary of Transnistria</a> were composed of around 4,500–7,500 soldiers, divided into four motorised infantry brigades in <a href="/wiki/Tiraspol" title="Tiraspol">Tiraspol</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bender,_Moldova" title="Bender, Moldova">Bender</a>, <a href="/wiki/R%C3%AEbni%C8%9Ba" title="Rîbnița">Rîbnița</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Dub%C4%83sari" title="Dubăsari">Dubăsari</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[89]</a></sup> They have 18 tanks, 107 armoured personnel carriers, 73 field guns, 46 anti-aircraft installations, and 173 tank destroyer units. The air force is composed of 9 Mi-8T helicopters, 6 Mi-24 helicopters, 2 Mi-2 helicopters, and several fixed-wing aircraft, including, An-2, An-26 and Yak-18 types.<sup id="cite_ref-armed1_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-armed1-91">[90]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-armed2_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-armed2-92">[91]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Transnistria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:SignInMoldovanCyrillic.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/SignInMoldovanCyrillic.JPG/220px-SignInMoldovanCyrillic.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="90" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/SignInMoldovanCyrillic.JPG/330px-SignInMoldovanCyrillic.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/SignInMoldovanCyrillic.JPG/440px-SignInMoldovanCyrillic.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1016" data-file-height="414"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:SignInMoldovanCyrillic.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Welcome (<i>Bine ați venit!</i>) sign in <a href="/wiki/Moldovan_Cyrillic" class="mw-redirect" title="Moldovan Cyrillic">Moldovan Cyrillic</a> in <a href="/wiki/Tiraspol" title="Tiraspol">Tiraspol</a>. The Cyrillic alphabet was replaced by the <a href="/wiki/Latin_alphabet" title="Latin alphabet">Latin alphabet</a> in 1989 in Moldova, but remains in use in Transnistria.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Moldova" title="Demographics of Moldova">Demographics of Moldova</a> and <a href="/wiki/Demographic_history_of_Transnistria" title="Demographic history of Transnistria">Demographic history of Transnistria</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:292px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Transnistria_evolutie_etnica.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Transnistria_evolutie_etnica.png/290px-Transnistria_evolutie_etnica.png" decoding="async" width="290" height="526" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Transnistria_evolutie_etnica.png/435px-Transnistria_evolutie_etnica.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Transnistria_evolutie_etnica.png/580px-Transnistria_evolutie_etnica.png 2x" data-file-width="1003" data-file-height="1820"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Transnistria_evolutie_etnica.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Demographic evolution in Transnistrian regions and the city of Tiraspol. Purple: Moldovan (Romanians), green: Ukrainians, blue: Russians.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2015_census">2015 census</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Transnistria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: 2015 census">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In October 2015, Transnistrian authorities organised <a href="/w/index.php?title=2015_Transnistrian_census&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="2015 Transnistrian census (page does not exist)">another separate census</a> from the <a href="/wiki/2014_Moldovan_Census" class="mw-redirect" title="2014 Moldovan Census">2014 Moldovan Census</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[92]</a></sup> According to the 2015 census, the population of the region was 475,373, a 14.47% decrease from the figure recorded at the 2004 census. The <a href="/wiki/Urbanization" title="Urbanization">urbanization</a> rate was 69.9%. By ethnic composition, the population of Transnistria was distributed as follows: Russians – 29.1%, Moldovans – 28.6%, Ukrainians – 22.9%, Bulgarians – 2.4%, Gagauzians – 1.1%, Belarusians – 0.5%, Transnistrian – 0.2%, other nationalities – 1.4%. About 14% of the population did not declare their nationality. Also, for the first time, the population had the option to identify as "Transnistrian".<sup id="cite_ref-2015census_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2015census-94">[93]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>According to another source, the largest ethnic groups in 2015 were 161,300 <a href="/wiki/Russians" title="Russians">Russians</a> (34%), 156,600 <a href="/wiki/Moldovans" title="Moldovans">Moldovans</a> (33%), and 126,700 <a href="/wiki/Ukrainians" title="Ukrainians">Ukrainians</a> (26.7%). <a href="/wiki/Bulgarians" title="Bulgarians">Bulgarians</a> comprised 13,300 (2.8%), <a href="/wiki/Gagauz_people" title="Gagauz people">Gagauz</a> 5,700 (1.2%) and <a href="/wiki/Belarusians" title="Belarusians">Belarusians</a> 2,800 (0.6%). <a href="/wiki/Germans" title="Germans">Germans</a> accounted for 1,400 or 0.3% and <a href="/wiki/Poles" title="Poles">Poles</a> for 1,000 or 0.2%. Others accounted for 5,700 people or 1.2%.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[94]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2004_census">2004 census</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Transnistria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: 2004 census">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In 2004, Transnistrian authorities organised <a href="/wiki/2004_Transnistrian_census" title="2004 Transnistrian census">a separate census</a> from the <a href="/wiki/2004_Moldovan_Census" class="mw-redirect" title="2004 Moldovan Census">2004 Moldovan Census</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[95]</a></sup> As per 2004 census, in the areas controlled by the PMR government, there were 555,347 people, including 177,785 <a href="/wiki/Moldovans" title="Moldovans">Moldovans</a> (32.10%) 168,678 <a href="/wiki/Russians" title="Russians">Russians</a> (30.35%) 160,069 <a href="/wiki/Ukrainians" title="Ukrainians">Ukrainians</a> (28.81%) 13,858 <a href="/wiki/Bulgarians" title="Bulgarians">Bulgarians</a> (2.50%) 4,096 <a href="/wiki/Gagauzians" class="mw-redirect" title="Gagauzians">Gagauzians</a> (0.74%), 1,791 <a href="/wiki/Poles" title="Poles">Poles</a> (0.32%), 1,259 <a href="/wiki/Jews" title="Jews">Jews</a> (0.23%), 507 <a href="/wiki/Romani_people" title="Romani people">Roma</a> (0.09%) and 27,454 others (4.94%).<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[96]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Of these, 439,243 lived in Transnistria itself, and 116,104 lived in localities controlled by the PMR government, but formally belonging to other districts of Moldova: the city of <a href="/wiki/Bender,_Moldova" title="Bender, Moldova">Bender</a> (Tighina), the communes of <a href="/wiki/Proteagailovca" title="Proteagailovca">Proteagailovca</a>, <a href="/wiki/G%C3%AEsca" title="Gîsca">Gîsca</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chi%C8%9Bcani,_Moldova" class="mw-redirect" title="Chițcani, Moldova">Chițcani</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cremenciug,_C%C4%83u%C8%99eni" title="Cremenciug, Căușeni">Cremenciug</a>, and the village of <i>Roghi</i> of commune <a href="/wiki/Molovata_Nou%C4%83" title="Molovata Nouă">Molovata Nouă</a>. </p>
      <p>Moldovans were the largest ethnic group, representing an overall majority in the two districts in the central Transnistria (<a href="/wiki/Dub%C4%83sari_District" title="Dubăsari District">Dubăsari District</a>, 50.15%, and <a href="/wiki/Grigoriopol_District" title="Grigoriopol District">Grigoriopol District</a>, 64.83%) a 47.82% relative majority in the northern <a href="/wiki/Camenca_District" title="Camenca District">Camenca District</a>, and a 41.52% relative majority in the southern (<a href="/wiki/Slobozia_District" title="Slobozia District">Slobozia District</a>). In Rîbnița District they were a 29.90% minority, and in the city of <a href="/wiki/Tiraspol" title="Tiraspol">Tiraspol</a>, they constituted a 15.24% minority of the population. </p>
      <p>As per last census, Russians were the second largest ethnic group, representing a 41.64% relative majority in the city of <a href="/wiki/Tiraspol" title="Tiraspol">Tiraspol</a>, a 24.07% minority in Slobozia, a 19.03% minority in Dubăsari, a 17.22% minority in Râbnița, a 15.28% minority in Grigoriopol, and a 6.89% minority in Camenca. </p>
      <p>Ukrainians were the third largest ethnic group, representing a 45.41% relative majority in the northern <a href="/wiki/R%C3%AEbni%C8%9Ba_District" title="Rîbnița District">Rîbnița District</a>, a 42.55% minority in Camenca, a 32.97% minority in Tiraspol, a 28.29% minority in Dubăsari, a 23.42% minority in Slobozia, and a 17.36% minority in Grigoriopol. A substantial number of Poles clustered in northern Transnistria were <a href="/wiki/Ukrainianization" class="mw-redirect" title="Ukrainianization">Ukrainianized</a> during Soviet rule. </p>
      <p>Bulgarians were the fourth largest ethnic group in Transnistria, albeit much less numerous than the three larger ethnicities. Most Bulgarians in Transnistria are <a href="/wiki/Bessarabian_Bulgarians" title="Bessarabian Bulgarians">Bessarabian Bulgarians</a>, descendants of expatriates who settled in <a href="/wiki/Bessarabia" title="Bessarabia">Bessarabia</a> in the 18th–19th century. The major centre of Bulgarians in Transnistria is the large village of <a href="/wiki/Parcani,_Transnistria" title="Parcani, Transnistria">Parcani</a> (situated between the cities of Tiraspol and Bender), which had an absolute Bulgarian majority and a total population of around 10,000. </p>
      <p>In Bender (Tighina) and the other non-<a href="/wiki/Transnistria_(geographical_region)" class="mw-redirect" title="Transnistria (geographical region)">Transnistria</a> localities under PMR control, ethnic Russians represented a 43.43% relative majority, followed by Moldovans at 26.15%, Ukrainians at 17.08%, Bulgarians at 2.89%, Gagauzians at 1.03%, Jews at 0.34%, Poles at 0.17%, Roma at 0.13%, and others at 7.78%. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1989_census">1989 census</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Transnistria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: 1989 census">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>At the <a href="/wiki/1989_Transnistrian_census" title="1989 Transnistrian census">census of 1989</a>, the population was 679,000 (including all the localities in the security zone, even those under Moldovan control). The ethnic composition of the region has <a href="/wiki/Demographic_history_of_Transnistria" title="Demographic history of Transnistria">been unstable in recent history</a>, with the most notable change being the decreasing share of Moldovan and Jewish population segments and increase of the Russian. For example, the percentage of Russians grew from 13.7% in 1926 to 25.5% in 1989 and further to 30.4% in 2004, while the Moldovan population decreased from 44.1% in 1926 to 39.9% in 1989 and 31.9% in 2004. Only the proportion of Ukrainians remained reasonably stable—27.2% in 1926, 28.3% in 1989 and 28.8 in 2004. </p>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Transnistria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Transnistria" title="Religion in Transnistria">Religion in Transnistria</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Noul_Neamts_monastery_is_located_5_km_from_Tiraspol_city_in_the_village_of_Chitcani._(15097599816).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Noul_Neamts_monastery_is_located_5_km_from_Tiraspol_city_in_the_village_of_Chitcani._%2815097599816%29.jpg/220px-Noul_Neamts_monastery_is_located_5_km_from_Tiraspol_city_in_the_village_of_Chitcani._%2815097599816%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Noul_Neamts_monastery_is_located_5_km_from_Tiraspol_city_in_the_village_of_Chitcani._%2815097599816%29.jpg/330px-Noul_Neamts_monastery_is_located_5_km_from_Tiraspol_city_in_the_village_of_Chitcani._%2815097599816%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Noul_Neamts_monastery_is_located_5_km_from_Tiraspol_city_in_the_village_of_Chitcani._%2815097599816%29.jpg/440px-Noul_Neamts_monastery_is_located_5_km_from_Tiraspol_city_in_the_village_of_Chitcani._%2815097599816%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4608" data-file-height="3456"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Noul_Neamts_monastery_is_located_5_km_from_Tiraspol_city_in_the_village_of_Chitcani._(15097599816).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Noul_Neam%C8%9B_Monastery" title="Noul Neamț Monastery">Noul Neamț Monastery</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>PMR official statistics show that 91% of the Transnistrian population adhere to <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Christianity" class="mw-redirect" title="Eastern Orthodox Christianity">Eastern Orthodox Christianity</a>, with 4% adhering to <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholicism">Roman Catholicism</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[98]</a></sup> Roman Catholics are mainly located in Northern Transnistria, where a notable <a href="/wiki/Poles" title="Poles">Polish</a> minority is living.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[99]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Transnistria's government has supported the restoration and construction of new Orthodox churches. It affirms that the republic has <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_religion" title="Freedom of religion">freedom of religion</a> and states that 114 religious beliefs and congregations are officially registered. However, as recently as 2005, registration hurdles were met with by some religious groups, notably the <a href="/wiki/Jehovah%27s_Witnesses" title="Jehovah's Witnesses">Jehovah's Witnesses</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[100]</a></sup> In 2007, the US-based <a href="/wiki/Christian_Broadcasting_Network" title="Christian Broadcasting Network">Christian Broadcasting Network</a> denounced the persecution of <a href="/wiki/Protestantism" title="Protestantism">Protestants</a> in Transnistria.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[101]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Transnistria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>Transnistria has a <a href="/wiki/Mixed_economy" title="Mixed economy">mixed economy</a>. Following a large scale <a href="/wiki/Privatisation" class="mw-redirect" title="Privatisation">privatisation</a> process in the late 1990s,<sup id="cite_ref-icg_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-icg-103">[102]</a></sup> most of the companies in Transnistria are now privately owned. The economy is based on a mix of <a href="/wiki/Heavy_industry" title="Heavy industry">heavy industry</a> (steel production), electricity production, and <a href="/wiki/Manufacturing" title="Manufacturing">manufacturing</a> (textile production), which together account for about 80% of the total industrial output.<sup id="cite_ref-viitorul_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-viitorul-104">[103]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:PMRcentralbank.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/PMRcentralbank.jpg/220px-PMRcentralbank.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="166" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/4/4c/PMRcentralbank.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="289" data-file-height="218"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:PMRcentralbank.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Transnistria's central bank, the Transnistrian Republican Bank
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Transnistria has its own central bank, the <a href="/wiki/Transnistrian_Republican_Bank" title="Transnistrian Republican Bank">Transnistrian Republican Bank</a>, which issues its national currency, the <a href="/wiki/Transnistrian_ruble" title="Transnistrian ruble">Transnistrian ruble</a>. It is convertible at a freely floating exchange rate but only in Transnistria. </p>
      <p>Transnistria's economy is frequently described as dependent on <a href="/wiki/Contraband" title="Contraband">contraband</a><sup id="cite_ref-An_illegal_business_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-An_illegal_business-105">[104]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Gunrunning" class="mw-redirect" title="Gunrunning">gunrunning</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Ющенко_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ющенко-106">[105]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Hotbed_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hotbed-107">[106]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Приднестровье_самоизолировалось_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Приднестровье_самоизолировалось-108">[107]</a></sup> with some labelling it a <a href="/wiki/Mafia_state" title="Mafia state">mafia state</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ДНЕСТРОВСКИЕ_ПОРОГИ_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ДНЕСТРОВСКИЕ_ПОРОГИ-109">[108]</a></sup> These allegations are denied by the Transnistrian government, and sometimes downplayed by the officials of Russia and Ukraine.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[109]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Economic_history">Economic history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Transnistria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Economic history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>After World War II, Transnistria was heavily industrialised, to the point that, in 1990, it was responsible for 40% of Moldova's GDP and 90% of its electricity,<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[110]</a></sup> although it accounted for only 17% of Moldova's population. After the collapse of the Soviet Union, Transnistria wanted to return to a "Brezhnev-style <a href="/wiki/Planned_economy" title="Planned economy">planned economy</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[111]</a></sup> However, several years later, it decided to head toward a <a href="/wiki/Market_economy" title="Market economy">market economy</a>. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:%D0%9F%D0%BB%D0%BE%D1%89%D0%B0%D0%B4%D1%8C_%D0%A1%D1%83%D0%B2%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B0_%D0%BF%D0%BE%D1%81%D0%BB%D0%B5_%D0%BF%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%B4%D0%B0.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/%D0%9F%D0%BB%D0%BE%D1%89%D0%B0%D0%B4%D1%8C_%D0%A1%D1%83%D0%B2%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B0_%D0%BF%D0%BE%D1%81%D0%BB%D0%B5_%D0%BF%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%B4%D0%B0.jpg/220px-%D0%9F%D0%BB%D0%BE%D1%89%D0%B0%D0%B4%D1%8C_%D0%A1%D1%83%D0%B2%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B0_%D0%BF%D0%BE%D1%81%D0%BB%D0%B5_%D0%BF%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%B4%D0%B0.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/%D0%9F%D0%BB%D0%BE%D1%89%D0%B0%D0%B4%D1%8C_%D0%A1%D1%83%D0%B2%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B0_%D0%BF%D0%BE%D1%81%D0%BB%D0%B5_%D0%BF%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%B4%D0%B0.jpg/330px-%D0%9F%D0%BB%D0%BE%D1%89%D0%B0%D0%B4%D1%8C_%D0%A1%D1%83%D0%B2%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B0_%D0%BF%D0%BE%D1%81%D0%BB%D0%B5_%D0%BF%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%B4%D0%B0.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/%D0%9F%D0%BB%D0%BE%D1%89%D0%B0%D0%B4%D1%8C_%D0%A1%D1%83%D0%B2%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B0_%D0%BF%D0%BE%D1%81%D0%BB%D0%B5_%D0%BF%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%B4%D0%B0.jpg/440px-%D0%9F%D0%BB%D0%BE%D1%89%D0%B0%D0%B4%D1%8C_%D0%A1%D1%83%D0%B2%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B0_%D0%BF%D0%BE%D1%81%D0%BB%D0%B5_%D0%BF%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%B4%D0%B0.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2100" data-file-height="1395"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
